                                                                               GROUNDS MUNITIONS




ACCESSIBILITY:         Publications and forms are available for downloading or ordering on the e-Pub-
                       lishing website at www.e-Publishing.af.mil (will convert to
                       www.af.mil/e-publishing on AF Link)
RELEASABILITY: There are no releasability restrictions on this publication.


OPR: HQ AFSFC/SFXR                                                       Certified by: HQ USAF/XOS-F
                                                                              (Brig Gen Mary K. Hertog)
Supersedes AFCAT21-209V1, 3 February 2004                                                   Pages: 177

This catalog supports Air Force Policy Directive (AFPD) 21-2, Non-nuclear and Nuclear Munitions, and
is used in concert with Air Force Catalog (AFCAT) 21-209, Volume 2, Demolition Munitions. This pub-
lication is the primary munitions authorization source that units and command functional areas use to
forecast ground munitions needs. Units and command functional areas must use AFCAT 21-209, Volume
2, when forecasting demolition munitions needs (i.e. blasting caps, demolition blocks, dynamite, etc.).
This catalog contains operational and training munitions authorizations and explains how these authoriza-
tions are established, reviewed and changed. Justification referenced in other Air Force and or major com-
mand (MAJCOM) directives listing munitions requirements will be provided to the appropriate authority,
if applicable. It provides general information on establishing, changing and estimating operational and
training munitions authorizations; explains how to forecast proper category codes, maintain expenditure
data and provides special instructions for munitions authorizations; provides munitions authorizations for
training, exercises, evaluations and competitions; and provides munitions authorizations for peacetime
security, war and contingency operations, and mobility. Send comments and suggested improvements on
AF Form 847, Recommendation for Change of Publication, through command channels to HQ AFSFC/
SFXR, 1517 Billy Mitchell Blvd, Lackland AFB TX 78236-0119. Activities must send implementing
publications to the higher headquarters functional OPR for review and coordination before publishing.
The OPR of AFCAT 21-209, volume 1, determines and grants waiver for any part of this publication.
Ensure all records created as a result of processes prescribed in this publication are maintained in accor-
dance with AFMAN 37-123, management of Records and disposed of in accordance with the Air Force
Records Disposition Schedule (RDS) located at https://afrims.amc.af.mil/.

SUMMARY OF CHANGES
This document has been substantially revised and must be completely reviewed.

                                               Chapter 1

                                     GENERAL INFORMATION

1.1. Establishing Munitions Authorizations. Units or functions responsible for an operational mission or
training program will send requests to create a munitions authorization to the parent MAJCOM munitions
users functional managers (MUFM). Each request will:
   1.1.1. Contain complete explanation of the need for the specific munitions. Include computational
   methodology as to how the requirement was determined (i.e., operational mission [air base defense
   basic quantity] or training [number of students or classes] x [amount of munitions] x [number of
   classes or sessions per year].)
   1.1.2. Include annual requirement for each munitions type.
   1.1.3. State if requirement is an increase or decrease over previous requirements. Include previous
   year’s consumption reports.
   1.1.4. State when munitions are required.
   1.1.5. Be reviewed and validated by the MUFM. The requesting MAJCOM MUFM must coordinate
   request with all affected MAJCOMs MUFM and serving munitions staff for their concurrence and
   comments. The requesting MAJCOM will send the request with affected MAJCOMs comments and
   concurrence to the Air Staff functional manager (ASFM) for consideration. The ASFM sends
   approved request to HQ AFSFC/SFXR, 1517 Billy Mitchell Blvd, Lackland AFB TX 78236-0119 for
   coordination and inclusion in AFCAT 21-209v1. The ASFM sends disapproved requests to submit-
   ting MAJCOMs with an informational copy to affected MAJCOMs and HQ AFSFC for their informa-
   tion and possible action. If the user does not have a MUFM, the supporting MAJCOM staff director
   will appoint one in writing that will coordinate requests through the servicing MAJCOM munitions
   staff before forwarding to HQ AFSFC/SFXR.

1.2. Changing Authorizations. Be reviewed and validated by the MUFM. The requesting MAJCOM
MUFM must coordinate request with all affected MAJCOMs MUFM and serving munitions staff for their
concurrence and comments. The requesting MAJCOM will send the request with affected MAJCOMs
comments and concurrence to the ASFM for consideration. The ASFM sends approved requests to HQ
AFSFC/SFXR, 1517 Billy Mitchell Blvd, Lackland AFB TX 78236-0119 for coordination and inclusion
in AFCAT 21-209v1. The ASFM sends disapproved requests to submitting MAJCOMs with an informa-
tional copy to affected MAJCOMs and HQ AFSFC for their information and possible action.
   1.2.1. Units may request one-time authorizations for items needed for special projects, missions, or
   training not covered by this publication.
   1.2.2. Units may request interim changes to a munitions authorization.
   1.2.3. Each request will include computation methodology on how the new requirement was deter-
   mined.

1.3. Developing Requirements Forecasts. Use the authorizations in this catalog to develop annual muni-
tions forecasts. Each activity responsible for an operational mission or for providing training with muni-
tions will:
16                                                               AFCAT21-209V1 9 NOVEMBER 2007


     1.3.1. Determine type and quantity of munitions needed to support peacetime and contingency needs.
     1.3.2. Determine number of participants or classes requiring training during the forecast period and
     compute required munitions quantities.
     1.3.3. Provides total munitions requirement as directed by the MUFM, in accordance with AFI
     21-201, Management and Maintenance of Non-Nuclear Munitions, Chapter 13. MUFM will validate
     forecasted munitions requirements and alibis for all munitions users. Validated forecasts will be for-
     warded to the MAJCOM munitions staffs. As a minimum, during requirement validation, consider
     past expenditure rates, force structure, arming policies and mission changes. MAJCOM munitions
     staffs verify data elements such as complete round codes, Department of Defense (DoD) identification
     codes and national stock numbers (NSN) on the MUFM forecasts.

1.4. Records and Reports. Records and reports of munitions expended are used to establish, validate and
fund forecast submissions. Use these records and reports of past munitions expenditures to establish real-
istic forecasts in support of future operational and training requirements. MUFM should keep a copy of
their submitted forecasts.

1.5. Training Requirements Validation. MUFM will review the ground munitions forecast and ensure
Category D (training) requirements are consistent with historical expenditure data. MUFM will also jus-
tify and prepare alibis for any requirements that have changed by plus or minus 10% from the previous
year’s validated requirement.

1.6. Special Instructions.
     1.6.1. To use or procure commercial off-the-shelf (COTS) explosives and munitions, requesting units
     must process the request and comply with the guidance in AFI 21-201, Chapter 32.
     1.6.2. If training conditions do not permit use of identified munitions, MAJCOMs may authorize
     units to forecast for substitute items (e.g., approved units may forecast for and use 7.62mm ball in lieu
     of 7.62mm tracer due to fire hazards on their training ranges.)
     1.6.3. Munitions requirements forecast categories: Refer to AFI 21-201, Management and Mainte-
     nance of Non-Nuclear Munitions, for applicable information on munitions category and requirement
     codes.

1.7. Lead Time for Delivery of Munitions. New or increased munitions requirements can take two or
more years after forecast before items are available. Programming, approval, funding and procurement
actions make up this lead-time. The Air Force's ability to support operational and training requirements is
directly dependent upon the timeliness and accuracy of forecasts. Munitions users should order only what
they can use and use what they order. By following this simple methodology, end-of-year munitions
excess will be minimal.
 AFCAT21-209V1 9 NOVEMBER 2007                                                                        17


                                               Chapter 2

                           TRAINING MUNITIONS AUTHORIZATIONS

 Section 2A—Headquarters US Air Force Directed Training, Exercise, Competition and Weapons
 Maintenance Authorizations

 2.1. General Information. Munitions authorized in Chapter 2 are for training, exercises, evaluations and
 competitions. They are maximum authorizations and functional managers should consider factors such as
 storage requirements when preparing munitions forecasts.

 2.2. Munitions Authorizations for Training, Exercises, Evaluations and Competitions. Foreign govern-
 ment students or personnel from any branch, department or activity of the US Government attached to the
 Air Force as students (including Air Force Reserve Officer Training Corps (AFROTC)) for training
 receive the same authorizations as Air Force personnel.

     person authorizations and in addition to authorizations in succeeding sections. (OPR: HQ AFSFC/
     SFXR)

                                                  Chapter 3

                          OPERATIONAL MUNITIONS AUTHORIZATIONS

Section 3A—Security Forces and Air Force Office of Special Investigations Munitions Authorizations

3.1. General Information. Munitions authorized in Chapter 3 are for operational peacetime, wartime and
contingency missions. They are the maximum authorizations, and functional managers should consider
factors such as storage requirements when preparing munitions forecasts.

3.2. Definitions.
      3.2.1. Fighting Load (FL): The munitions quantity supervisors decide to issue to individuals or gun
      crews for armed duty. This is normally the munitions quantity individuals carry on their persons or
      gun crews have immediately available. Functional managers, commands and supervisors determine
      fighting load quantities. FL is normally supported from basic quantity stocks during the first few days
      of an operation. Sustaining quantity is used if necessary for subsequent support.
      3.2.2. Basic Quantity (BQ): The munitions quantity authorized to establish a stockpile from which to
      issue FLs to persons and gun crews performing armed duty. BQ normally accompanies deploying
      forces; therefore, supporting commands forecast and provide basic quantities of ammunition.
      3.2.3. Sustaining Quantity (SQ): The prepositioned quantity of specific munitions authorized to
      establish a resupply stockpile. Supported commands forecast for and preposition munitions sustaining
      quantities based on threat analysis or possible resupply difficulties.

3.3. Security Forces and USAF Office of Special Investigations (AFOSI) Munitions Authorizations.
      3.3.1. For Protection of Air Force Installations, Equipment and Personnel. (OPR: HQ AFSFC/SFO
      and AFOSI/XPP) These munitions are separate and in addition to air base defense authorizations.
      They are to establish operating levels for security forces and Air Force Office of Special Investiga-
      tions functions to include Antiterrorism Specialty Teams (AST), other than CENTAF (SF forces do
      not participate in AST), and other threat teams.
